<review>This is one of my (if not my absolute) favourite filipino restaurants in SF. I came across it pretty much by accident when I was looking for filipino food, not having heard of it beforel It's located in TL which isn't the greatest, but it's not a deal breaker (plus, if the location was really an issue for you, they're available on some food delivery platforms). Upon entering, it already felt "familiar" in a way that other filipino restaurants in SF didn't. It felt homey and the staff were friendly and kinda reminded me of my aunties; they were helpful too, especially when they (probably) saw the overwhelmed look on my and my bf's faces when seeing the lengthy menu. Eventually (and multiple times since that first visit) I settled on the tapsilog and it has become one of my favourite things to get here... that, and the lumpia. Can't argue with the classics ;) The last time I was here, I brought some of my filipina friends with me and they liked the food too, especially the lechon. < user_name>
Vernon Sanders< /user_name>
<time>1502084550030</time>< rate>
5<//rate>
< text>
The staff is friendly. They have a variety of dishes on rotation, and I've never tried one that I didn't like. The prices are reasonable as well. I'm not quite sure why Filipino food never took off like Thai, or even Burmese, food has. But if you haven't had much Filipino food this is a great place to try. They serve accessible dishes like adobo and bisteak.  They also offer dishes for those who want to try food that sharply departs from standard American fare, such as dinuguan and pig ear sisig. Finally, don't be put off by the location. It's worth it.</text>

April Diaz</Name>
<Time>1392935278731<//Time><rate>4<//rate><Review>There aren't a lot of Filipino restaurants in the city that I like. With a decent population of Filipinos, you would think there would be more options, but there isn't. I often have to venture out. But Kusina Ni Tess is one of my downtown spots when I need my fix. It's a cheap turo-turo place. Turo-turo literally means "point-point". Obviously, you point at the food you want. But I mean you can still talk and ask questions, as most people there speak English.

They have a good deal for about $7-8 bucks for a two item meal with rice. You can also ask for a free side of sabow (soup broth, usually nilaga or sinigang broth). I like the adobos and the paksiws. I usually come here with my boyfriend, and that two item meal ends up being enough for the both of us. $7-8  for two people? Sheeet. What a steal!<//Review><Pics>None< /Pics>< response>

< Text>
Very nice place to go get the things that you need in a jiffy. Not only is Trader Joe's in this Shopping Center but Smart & Final as well as Grocery Outlet are all conveniently located in the same vicinity. Did I mention Dimple Records is also in this Roseville Square. The staff there was very friendly and very knowledgeable. I took in some CDs that I will no longer be listening to thanks to Apple music and I got paid cash for them the very same day. They also buy vinyl records, cassette tapes, and DVD's. They buy video games and consoles and also sell them at reasonable prices. I would highly recommend taking any of your unwanted media to Dimple Records... Trader Joes also has a decent size selection of of flowers that are in bloom!<//Text>

<Name>Drew Sharp</Name>< review>
Hard to imagine back in the day this used to be Rosevilles mall. Times have changed and so has the kinds of stores offered here. Check out the discount grocery deals at Groccery Outlet, get a yummy treat at Starbucks, a Cool 50s /60s dinner is a local favorite, other stores include Rite Aid, Trader Joe's, 2 banks, Subway, and the new home of Dimples Music. Something for everyone. Just 2 bad things. (1) The parking is crazy here and can be a Mad House on the weekends. TIP: park in the back by the Senior Housing. (2) There is a, high at times homeless/ pan handler/  druggie element here.</review>

< text>
They have been trying for years to bring this shopping center back from the dead. They've remodeled most of the buildings now and there are several good businesses in the center, but still a lot of little vacancies and low traffic on the Southern end of the center. I would love to see this place back 100%. The parking here is awkward, cramped and very poorly laid out. Notable businesses are Trader Joes, Smart and Final, Bank of America, Grocery Outlet, Rite Aid, Banfield Veterinary, Any Mountain Sporting Goods and Chase Bank.</text>
